Think about it — when was the last time you looked forward to showing off your underarms during summer? Probably never.</p><p>That's because, aside from being totally unexciting, underarms are often ignored, under-pampered, and in less-than-peak condition. That's exactly why <a href=\"https://ulta.ztk5.net/c/196318/164999/3037?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ulta.com%2Fhealthy-underarm-detox-mask%3FproductId%3DxlsImpprod17441013\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Lavanila's The Healthy Underarm Detox Mask</a> is such a unique find.</p><p>The all-natural mask is designed to remove buildup from traditional antiperspirants and deodorants, brighten dull or uneven skin tone, and help shorten the transitional period between traditional (read: chemical) antiperspirants to more natural picks. &#160;</p><h2>The ingredients</h2><p>There are three major natural ingredients at play in this product — active charcoal, malic acid, and silica.</p><p>Active charcoal exfoliates to remove toxins and impurities, brightening the skin. Malic acid then works like a magnet, binding to and removing aluminum and metal ions — which are ingredients found in traditional antiperspirants. Finally, silica steps in to absorb sweat molecules while nourishing skin, so rough, bumpy skin becomes more touchable.&#160;&#160;</p><h2>My experience with the mask</h2><p>There are a lot of ways a beauty company can mess up the packaging of a product regardless of where it goes on your body. It can be messy. It can be hard to scoop out the product. It can be hard to apply on your skin. It can be even harder to wash off.&#160;</p><p>It seemed like Lavanila knew all this because there are none of those issues here. The mask comes in an upside-down bottle (so there's no awkward squeezing or shaking to get the last of the product out) with a wide brush that applies the mask smoothly onto your underarms with absolutely no weird angling.</p><p>Seriously, the first time I used it, I was ready to spend about 15 minutes just applying the mask onto my skin. It took all of 90 seconds for both arms — and that's me being <em>really</em> slow.</p><p>But perhaps the most awkward part is waiting while the mask does its work on your skin. It only needs to sit for five minutes, but you have to spend that time with your arms awkwardly raised above your head or behind your back. I took this time to do some much-needed post-work meditation instead. Seriously, it's the perfect excuse to lie down for five whole minutes and literally do nothing because you don't want to mess up the mask.&#160;</p><p>Clean up was also surprisingly easy. Just as the directions say, all you need is a washcloth with warm water to wipe the mask off your skin. I mention this in awe because there are so many masks that claim to be easy to rinse and remove, but I find myself needing to hop in the shower in an effort to remove all of the dried out remains. No shower needed here though.</p><p><a href=\"https://ulta.ztk5.net/c/196318/164999/3037?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ulta.com%2Fhealthy-underarm-detox-mask%3FproductId%3DxlsImpprod17441013\" target=\"_blank\" title=\"The upside-down squeeze tube includes a wide applicator brush to apply the mask on underarm skin smoothly. Wait five minutes for the mask to dry and then wipe it off with a with warm washcloth.\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\"><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5cdb06f1021b4c6f354dc105?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Lavanila’s Healthy Underarm Detox\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The upside-down squeeze tube includes a wide applicator brush to apply the mask on underarm skin smoothly. Wait five minutes for the mask to dry and then wipe it off with a warm washcloth.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lavanila</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></a></p><h2>The results</h2><p><a href=\"https://ulta.ztk5.net/c/196318/164999/3037?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ulta.com%2Fhealthy-underarm-detox-mask%3FproductId%3DxlsImpprod17441013\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Lavanila's The Healthy Underarm Detox Mask</a> was designed with three major goals — help remove impurities (especially aluminum), shorten the transition period to natural deodorants, and brighten the underarm area.</p><p>Honestly, I had no desire to switch to a natural deodorant, but after just one week, I knew why this mask was so helpful for anyone who wanted to take that journey. I noticed that with each use, I sweated less and less. The skin on my underarms also became noticeably softer. It's a weird thing to think about, but for some reason, softer, smoother underarms gave me a tiny confidence boost.</p><p>Now, let's get to the real results I was looking for — brightening. Throughout the years, my underarm skin had become a bit discolored — something I knew stemmed from the buildup from my traditional antiperspirant — and had some less-than-desirable bumps. The one hope I had was for the mask to restore my skin to a happier state.</p><p>While my skin was not celebrity-level clean — seriously, how do stars get their underarms looking so smooth and even anyway? — I did see a noticeable difference after about two weeks of using the mask. It wasn't a night and day difference, but it was enough to give me a pretty good confidence boost, which is essential since I'll soon be trading in my long-sleeves for tank tops.</p><h2>Would I keep using it?</h2><p>In a word — yes. I plan to keep using the mask for the rest of the spring and summer. Its ability to minimize my sweating and brighten my underarm skin gave me a self-esteem boost I never knew I needed. Who knew I can be so emotionally affected by my underarms?&#160;</p><p>But at $26 for 1.5 oz., it's still a pretty steep price to pay several times a year, so I'll categorize this mask under must-have <em>summer</em> beauty products instead of year-round. I'll use it when I want to flaunt around in my favorite sleeveless sundress and bathing suit, and then save it when the cool weather sets in. It's not like anyone's going to stare at my underarms while I pick apples in the fall.</p><div id=\"ProductCard_5eb1c0ad204ad30fa414c857\" style=\"position:relative; display:block; width: 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"First-term Rep. Van Taylor, R-Texas, walks down the House steps after a vote on Wednesday, Sept. 18, 2019.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Bill Clark/CQ-Roll Call/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>First-term Rep. Van Taylor will face Democrat Lulu Seikaly to represent Texas' 3rd Congressional District.</li>\n<li>The 3rd District is located in northeastern Texas, just above Dallas. It is home&#160;to most of Collin County which includes the cities of McKinney, Plano, Frisco, and part of Dallas.&#160;</li>\n<li>In the 2016 presidential election, the district voted for President Donald Trump over Hillary Clinton by 14 points.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>First-term <strong>Rep. Van Taylor</strong> looks to defend his seat against Democratic challenger <strong>Lulu Seikaly</strong> in Texas' 3rd Congressional District.&#160;</p><h2>The candidates</h2><p>Taylor is a businessman and veteran of the U.S. Marine Corps Reserves where he was deployed in Iraq. He is a former state senator and state representative, serving in the Texas state legislature from 2011 to 2019. Taylor was elected to the House of Representatives in 2018 following 13-term Republican Rep. Sam Johnson's retirement. He currently sits on the powerful <a href=\"https://vantaylor.house.gov/about/committees-and-caucuses.htm\">House Committee on Financial Services</a>.</p><p>Seikaly is an attorney specializing in labor and employment law. She has <a href=\"https://lulufortexas.com/endorsements/\">received endorsements from</a> the Dallas Morning News in her Democratic primary bid (the paper has not yet endorsed a candidate for the general election), the Texas AFL-CIO, and Stonewall Democrats of Dallas.</p><p>Seikaly's <a href=\"https://lulufortexas.com/issues/\">campaign platform is focused on</a> reforming the healthcare system, universal prenatal care, demilitarizing police forces, and repealing mandatory minimum charges in the judicial system.</p><h2>The district</h2><p>Texas' 3rd Congressional District is located in northeastern Texas, directly northeast of Dallas. The district is home to most of Collin County which includes the cities of McKinney, Plano, Frisco, and part of Dallas.&#160;</p><p>This wealthy, suburban district <a href=\"https://demographics.texas.gov/Resources/Presentations/OSD/2019/2019_12_07_TexasMedicalAssociation.pdf\">has seen steady population growth</a> over the past several years, including a growing share of Asian-American and Latino residents. It has not been represented by a Democrat since Rep. Joe Pool's death in 1968.</p><p>In the 2016 presidential election, the 3rd District voted for Trump over Democratic nominee Hillary Clinton by nearly 14 points in a 55-41 percentage point split of the vote, according to the <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2013/07/09/1220127/-Daily-Kos-Elections-2012-election-results-by-congressional-and-legislative-districts\">Daily Kos</a>, after backing 2012 Republican nominee Mitt Romney by a much larger 30 percentage point margin over former President Barack Obama.&#160;</p><p>In <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1W_GTNylAZfboZkDeMsJPGlir3aQB64SzlVHjY9Xdnkk/edit#gid=562073942\">Texas' 2018 US Senate election</a>, the district backed Republican Senator Ted Cruz by a margin of three points, 51% to 48%, over Democratic challenger Beto O'Rourke.&#160;</p><h2>The money race</h2><p>According to the <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=TX03&spec=Np;spec=N\">Center for Responsive Politics</a>, Taylor has raised $1.6 million for his campaign, spent about $734,000, and currently has $1 million left to spend as the November election approaches. Conversely, Seikaly has raised $408,000, spent about $369,000, and has just $39,000 in cash on hand remaining.</p><h2>What experts say</h2><p>The race between Taylor and Seikaly is rated as \"safe Republican\" by <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections</a>, \"likely Republican\" by <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball</a> at the University of Virginia Center for Politics, and \"leans Republican\" by the <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a>.</p><bi-shortcode 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"What you need to know about North Carolina's governor race between Roy Cooper and Dan Forest","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/roy-cooper-vs-dan-forest-north-carolina-governor-election-2020","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f3f096542f43f001ddfe367?format=jpeg\" alt=\"RoyCooper-DanForest\" height=\"1600\" width=\"2560\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>North Carolina Gov. Roy Cooper/Lt. Gov. Dan Forest.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Ethan Hyman/Raleigh News &#38; Observer/Tribune News Service via Getty Images/Gerry Broome/AP Photo</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Democratic Gov. Roy Cooper is seeking a second term against his Republican challenger Lt. Gov. Dan Forest.</li>\n<li>Cooper has longtime served in politics whereas Forest's current office is the first he has held. Both are running on different approaches to handle the coronavirus pandemic.</li>\n<li>The latest polls and election experts rank Cooper ahead of Forest. Cooper's campaign has also outraised Forest's.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Republican Lt. Gov. <strong>Dan Forest</strong> is running to unseat Democratic Gov. <strong>Roy Cooper</strong>, who is seeking a second term.</p><h3><strong>The candidates:</strong></h3><p>In North Carolina, votes for governor and lieutenant governor are cast on separate ballots, meaning there is a possibility that the winners may be of different parties, as was the case in the 2016 election.</p><p>Cooper, a longtime elected official who previously served as state attorney general and a state legislator, ousted incumbent Republican Pat McCrory by a razor-thin margin, a mere 0.2 percentage points or roughly 10,000 votes.&#160;</p><p>Forest, a former businessman and architect, launched his political career when he was first elected in McCrory's term. He won his 2016 reelection by 6.6 points.&#160;</p><p>Cooper has focused his 2020 bid on how he would continue to handle COVID-19, including fighting for Medicaid expansion, an unsuccessful battle against the Republican-controlled state legislature during his tenure so far.&#160;</p><p>Forest has launched attacks at his opponent's leadership during the public health crisis and revolves around addressing the pandemic differently, such as an in-person schools reopening versus remote, echoing President Donald Trump's approach.</p><p>Trump threw his support behind Forest after blaming Cooper's event capacity limits as preventing him from hosting the Republican National Convention in Charlotte. The event, a mix of in-person and virtual gatherings, is still being held there, though Trump plans to accept his nomination from the White House.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">&#8212;Donald J. Trump  (@realDonaldTrump) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1278830005422874624?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 2, 2020</a></blockquote><script async src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>&#160;</p><p>Forest also sued Cooper in an <a href=\"https://apnews.com/a9baa8cc2a91deb3ce01a38e597c0dee\">attempt to block</a> such executive orders that closed businesses and limited mass gatherings, arguing he exceeded his constitutional authorities. A judge rejected his demand.&#160;</p><p>\"Dan Forest's lawsuit never had teeth and today's ruling confirms that,\" a Cooper spokesperson said. \"It was never more than a desperate tactic to garner attention for his political campaign. His time would be better spent putting the health and safety of North Carolinians before his own political motivations.\"</p><p>\"I did my part,\" Forest <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DanForestNC/status/1293291144433094656?s=20\">tweeted after the decision</a>. \"If y'all want your freedoms back you'll have to make your voices heard in November.\"</p><h3><strong>The stakes:</strong></h3><p>The 2020 gubernatorial contests are unlike recent election cycles considering the coronavirus pandemic. Eight out of the 11 races feature <a href=\"https://fivethirtyeight.com/features/2020-governors-races-update/\">incumbents seeking reelection</a>, including Cooper, who may have his fate decided based on his response.</p><p>Trump won North Carolina in 2016 by 3.6 percentage points, <a href=\"https://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/articles/the-governors-party-control-now-near-parity/\">one of eight states</a> that went red nationally but have blue governors. Should Forest win in 2020, all three of the state's branches of government will be under GOP control.&#160;</p><p>Other major elections in the state include the Senate race between incumbent <strong>Thom Tillis</strong> versus Democratic challenger <strong>Cal Cunningham</strong>, as well as open bids for the newly redrawn 6th Congressional District and 2nd Congressional District.</p><p><strong>The money race:&#160;</strong>Cooper has significantly outraised Forest since his reelection effort started in 2017, with more than $19 million. Forest last campaign finance filing in July was his best yet, <a href=\"https://apnews.com/8d797a862b8c3641f20b3ab0b334ff6e\">raising $2.4 million</a>, bringing his total to $6.9 million.&#160;</p><p><strong>What the polls say:&#160;</strong>Latest polling data show Cooper with a <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/governor/north-carolina/?states=ND\">huge 13-point advantage</a> over Forest, as of Aug. 16. The <a href=\"https://www.realclearpolitics.com/epolls/2020/governor/nc/north_carolina_governor_cooper_vs_forest-6750.html\">Real Clear Politics average</a> last updated in May places Cooper 17 points ahead of Forest.&#160;</p><p><strong>What the experts say:&#160;</strong>The race has been rated as lean Democratic by <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/governor-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a> and <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/governor\">Inside Elections</a> and likely Democratic by <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-governor/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball</a> at the University of Virginia Center for Politics.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article Here are 3 themes and 9 stocks he's betting on.</a></em></p><p>Tom Staggs, a former chief operating officer at Disney, will serve as the chair of the SPAC's strategic advisory committee. Salil Mehta, a former Disney strategy executive, will be Forest Road's chief financial officer. Kevin Mayer, a former TikTok CEO and chief strategy officer at Disney, will serve as a strategic advisor; Mayer also led the launch of Disney Plus in November.</p><p>The team's \"distinguished and long-term track record of sourcing, acquiring, and building next-generation media and entertainment platforms\" will aid the SPAC's leaders in providing \"differentiated consumer insights and sourcing opportunities,\" the filing said.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/stock-picks-to-buy-packaged-food-companies-covid-cooking-stifel-2020-10\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Buy these 7 stocks poised to profit from the boom in packaged-food sales as COVID-19 prompts more Americans to cook at home, Stifel says.</a></em></p><p>So-called blank-check companies raise cash through an initial public offering with the intention of merging with a private firm and taking the combined entity public. Investors who buy into a SPAC's IPO are typically in the dark as to what company will be targeted.</p><p>While some have hailed the vehicles as a better way to take companies public, others have said SPACs are too lightly regulated.</p><p>More than $53 billion has been raised across 138 SPAC debuts in 2020, trouncing the $13.6 billion raised last year, <a href=\"https://spacinsider.com/stats/\">according to SPACInsider.com</a>. 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Republican Darrell Issa and Democrat Ammar Campa Najjar battle for the open seat in California's 50th Congressional District","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/california-50th-district-house-election-ammar-campa-najjar-darrell-issa-020","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5fa64e323fc4001e0d60dd?format=jpeg\" alt=\"voting ballot box california\" height=\"1798\" width=\"3596\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>An official ballot drop box is set up in Los Angeles on September 12, 2020, ahead of the November 3 presidential elections.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Chris DELMAS/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Republican Darrell Issa and Democrat Ammar Campa-Najjar will face each other in November to represent California's 50th Congressional District.</li>\n<li>The 50th District is located in southern California and is home to the northeastern and central regions of San Diego County as well as a portion of Riverside County.&#160;</li>\n<li>The House seat is currently vacant after Rep. Duncan Hunter resigned after pleading guilty for conspiracy misuse of campaign funds.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Republican <strong>Darrell Issa</strong> and Democrat <strong>Ammar Campa-Najjar</strong> face off this November to represent California's 50th Congressional District.</p><p>Former GOP Rep. Duncan Hunter represented the district for nearly four terms in Congress but became embroiled in a scandal when federal prosecutors <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2019/12/03/us/duncan-hunter-guilty-plea.html\">charged him and his wife Margaret</a> with over 60 counts of embezzling campaign funds, wire fraud, falsification of campaign finance records, and conspiracy.</p><p>Duncan lost his committee assignments upon being indicted, and submitted <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/california-rep-duncan-hunter-announces-resignation-2020-1\">letters of resignation</a> to both House Speaker Nancy Pelosi and Gov. Gavin Newsom a month after pleading guilty. Hunter resigned too late for Newsom to call a special election, leaving the seat vacant. In March, Hunter <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2020/03/17/us/duncan-hunter-sentencing.html\">was sentenced to 11 months in federal prison.</a></p><p>California currently has a&#160;<a href=\"https://www.sos.ca.gov/elections/primary-elections-california/\">\"top-two primary\"</a> system, meaning that the top two winners of the primary election go on the final ballot, regardless of their political party.</p><h2>The candidates</h2><p>Issa is a former US House representative who once represented the 48th and 49th districts, which both include portions of Orange County and are now represented by Democrats.</p><p>He is the co-founder and former CEO of Directed Electronics, one of the largest automobile security companies in the U.S. With an estimated net worth of $250 million, Issa was the <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/zackfriedman/2018/03/30/congress-money-entrepreneur/#50bdfd713c5a\">richest member of Congress</a> during his tenure. <a href=\"https://www.darrellissa.com/issues/\">His 2020 campaign platform</a> emphasizes building on a wall on the southern border, opposing illegal immigration and sanctuary cities, and creating fairer trade policies.&#160;</p><p>In late 2018, several months after announcing he was not seeking reelection, Issa was nominated by President Donald Trump to become the director of the United States Trade and Development Agency. In California's \"top-two primary\" in March, Issa <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/2020-election/results/california/\">placed second behind Campa-Najjar</a>.</p><p>Campa-Najjar is the deputy regional field director for President Barack Obama's reelection campaign and served a role in the Executive Office of the President.</p><p>He later became the <a href=\"https://www.campacampaign.com/meet-ammar\">communications and marketing director</a>&#160;for the United States Hispanic Chamber of Commerce and led the Office of Public Affairs for the Employment and Training Administration in the U.S. Department of Labor.</p><p>In 2018, Campa-Najjar ran against Rep. Hunter and narrowly <a href=\"https://elections.cdn.sos.ca.gov/sov/2018-general/sov/2018-complete-sov.pdf\">lost by a margin of 3.4 percentage points</a>. His <a href=\"https://www.campacampaign.com/\">2020 campaign platform</a> focuses on helping Southern California recover from the COVID-19 pandemic, expanding access to affordable healthcare, and increasing economic opportunity and supporting small businesses in the district.&#160;</p><h2>The district</h2><p>California's 50th Congressional District is located in the state's southern region and is home to the northeastern and central regions of San Diego County as well as a portion of Riverside County.&#160;</p><p>The district has traditionally been solidly Republican. For the 2016 presidential election, the 50th Congressional District voted for President Trump over Democratic candidate Hillary Clinton in a 55-40 percentage point split of the vote, <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2013/7/9/1220127/-Daily-Kos-Elections-2012-election-results-by-congressional-and-legislative-districts\">according to the Daily Kos</a>.</p><h2>The money race</h2><p>According to the <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=CA50&spec=Np;spec=N\">Center for Responsive Politics</a>, Issa has raised about $5.5 million, spent $5 million, and currently has $515,000 in cash on hand as the November election approaches. Campa-Najjar has raised approximately $3 million for his campaign, spent $2 million, and has $890,000 left to spend.&#160;</p><h2>What experts say</h2><p>The race between Issa and Campa-Najjar is rated as \"likely Republican\" by <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections</a>, the <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a>, and <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball</a> at the University of Virginia Center for Politics.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" look","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-san-jose-campus-renderings-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f80784f4c3b2e0019bba1ea?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Google San Jose\" height=\"719\" width=\"958\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Google San Jose campus.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Google</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Google just released renderings of a proposed new campus it hopes to build in San Jose, called Downtown West.</li>\n<li>Unlike other Google campuses, the San Jose location would be mixed-use and open to the public.</li>\n<li>The 79-acre area plan includes housing, office space, and nature areas, and is a major move by Google at a time when companies are rethinking office space needs in light of the pandemic forcing the workforce to work remotely.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Google released some new details about its planned San Jose campus on Thursday, with <a href=\"https://realestate.withgoogle.com/sanjose/updates/5674624803930112/share-your-thoughts-on-a-few-illustrations-of-downtown-west/\">renderings</a> and a <a href=\"https://www.sanjoseca.gov/Home/ShowDocument?id=65124\">473 slide deck.&#160;</a></p><p>The renderings give an idea of how Google envisions the new campus, with more detailed information in the slide deck produced for the city of San Jose. It will encompass far more than the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/google-los-angeles-office-wooden-airplane-hangar-photos-2019-11\">quirky office style</a> that Google is known for: there are plans for up to 5,900 residencies, retail spaces, pop-up events, and publicly accessible nature through trails and paths.&#160;</p><p>The design seems to consciously base itself off of aspects of San Jose that already exist. The Los Gatos Creek is highlighted in a larger nature area, and Google details plans to follow San Jose's climate change initiative by designing large open spaces to combat urban heat islands, accessible public transportation, and a possible onsite wastewater collection and recycling facility. Now, Google is asking for resident feedback before the plan is considered for approval by the San Jose city council in the spring.</p><p>Some big tech companies aren't slowing down their real estate plans this year, despite the pandemic. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/facebook-just-bought-reis-abandoned-seattle-area-hq-2020-9\">Facebook paid $376.6 million for REI's former unfinished Seattle-era headquarters</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.geekwire.com/2020/real-hq2-amazon-add-another-10000-jobs-bellevue-wash-nearby-downtown-seattle-hq/\">Amazon just leased two million additional square feet of office space</a> in Bellevue.</p><p>Meanwhile, as more work shifts remote <a href=\"https://www.sfchronicle.com/business/article/Pinterest-cancels-huge-SF-office-lease-in-unbuilt-15523170.php\">Pinterest canceled a large San Francisco lease</a>, and Twitter is trying to sublet parts of its San Francisco headquarters after telling workers <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitter-subleasing-san-francisco-headquarters-employees-work-from-home-2020-9\">they can work from home indefinitely</a>.</p><p>Take a look inside Google's plans here.&#160;</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe 79-acre campus would be a workplace for 25,000 employees.\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5b90b07ed0ee001e25ec67?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ben Ray Lujan .JPG\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>U.S. Representative Ben Ray Lujan speaks about unaccompanied minor shelters during a round table discussion in Brownsville, Texas, U.S. June 18, 2018.\n<p class=\"copyright\">REUTERS/Callaghan O&#39;Hare</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Rep. Ben Ray Luj&#225;n and Republican Mark Ronchetti are facing off for US Senate in New Mexico.</li>\n<li>Luj&#225;n has represented New Mexico's 3rd District since 2009, and has served as chairman of the Democratic Congressional Campaign Committee and House Assistant Democratic Leader.</li>\n<li>So far, Luj&#225;n has outraised Ronchetti by a nearly five-to-one ratio and is expected by win election to the seat in this largely Democratic state.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Democratic&#160;<strong>Rep. Ben Ray Luján</strong> is facing off against Republican&#160;<strong>Mark Ronchetti&#160;</strong>for US Senate in New Mexico.&#160;</p><h2><strong>The candidates:</strong></h2><p>Luján has represented New Mexico's 3rd Congressional District, which includes the Northern part of the state and the state's capital of Santa Fe, for over a decade since 2009. He previously served on New Mexico's Public Regulation Commission.&#160;</p><p>In the House, Luján has taken on leadership positions as chairman of the Democratic Congressional Campaign Committee, House' Democrats campaign arm, from 2015 to 2019, and now as the House Assistant Democratic Leader, making him currently the highest-ranking Hispanic member of the House.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Luján announced his candidacy for US Senate in 2019 shortly after current&#160;<strong>Sen. Mark Udall&#160;</strong>announced his retirement, and quickly cleared the field to secure the Democratic nomination.&#160;</p><p>His <a href=\"https://benraylujan.com/priorities/\">campaign platform emphasizes</a> investing in New Mexico families and improving opportunities and outcomes for children, strengthening New Mexico's economy, especially at New Mexico's bases and National Labs, and protecting New Mexico's natural resources and public lands.&#160;</p><p>Ronchetti, the Republican candidate, is a former TV news reporter and meteorologist in Albuquerque. <a href=\"https://www.markronchetti.com/issues\">His campaign platform</a> emphasizes lowering taxes and bringing more economic development to New Mexico, protecting 2nd Amendment rights, and bolstering security along the US' southern border.&#160;</p><h2>The stakes:</h2><p>In addition to winning back the White House, regaining control of the US Senate for the first time since 2015 is a top priority for Democrats and would be a major accomplishment towards either delivering on a future president Joe Biden's policy goals or thwarting President Donald Trump's second-term agenda.</p><p>Currently, the US Senate is made up of 53 Republicans, 45 Democrats, and two independents that caucus with Democrats, winning that Democrats need to win back a net total of four seats to have a 51-seat majority (if Biden wins, his vice president would also serve as president of the Senate and would be a tie-breaker vote).&#160;</p><p>New Mexico is a largely Democratic state, and Luján is currently favored to win election to the seat.</p><p>In the 2018 midterm elections as Luján was leading the DCCC, Democratic Rep. Xochitl Torres Small flipped New Mexico's 2nd Congressional District back into Democratic hands, and is facing a tough reelection rematch against Republican Yvette Herrell.&#160;</p><p><strong>The money race:&#160;</strong>Lujan has outraised Ronchetti by a nearly five-to-one-ratio, <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=NMS2NMS2\">according to the Center for Responsive Politics.</a> Lujan has brought in $6.1 million, spent $3.2 million, and has over $3.3 million cash on hand. Ronchetti has raised $1.38 million, spent over $809,000, and has $570,000 in cash on hand.&#160;</p><p><strong>What the polling says: </strong>The most recent poll of the race <a href=\"https://www.abqjournal.com/1493963/journal-poll-lujan-leads-ronchetti-in-us-senate-race.html\">conducted by the Albuquerque Journal and Research &#38; Polling Inc</a>. between August 26 and September 2 found Lujan leading Ronchetti by nine points, 49% to 40%.&#160;</p><p><strong>What some of the experts say:</strong> The <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/senate-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a> and <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/senate\">Inside Elections</a> rate the race between Smith and Lewis as \"safe Democratic\" while <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-senate/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball at the University of Virginia Center for Politics</a> rates it \"likely Democratic.\"&#160;</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/2020-election-forecast/senate/new-mexico/\">FiveThirtyEight</a>, Luján has a 95% chance of defeating Ronchetti in November and is expected to receive 14.6% more of the popular vote than his opponents.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f809c4cea74820019ca6429?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Former Vice President Joe Biden\" height=\"750\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Former Vice President Joe Biden\n<p class=\"copyright\">Mark Makela/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>A Democratic sweep in November would place stocks on a rollercoaster ride through the end of the year, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ms-stock\">Morgan Stanley</a> strategists said Friday.</strong></li><li><strong>US equities are among the few assets poised for a \"detour\" should a so-called blue wave take place. The market's steady climb would reverse temporarily before correcting in 2021, the analysts said.</strong></li><li><strong>Stocks would initially dip on fears of higher corporate taxes and uncertainty around future stimulus, according to the bank.</strong></li><li><strong>Once the party can clarify its fiscal relief plans, a follow-up to March's CARES Act and continued economic recovery can place stocks back on their upward path, the strategists added.&#160;</strong></li><li><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestutm_source=msn.com&utm_medium=referral&utm_content=msn-slideshow&utm_campaign=bodyurl?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestts&#38;utm_medium=ingest\">Visit the Business Insider homepage for more stories</a>.</strong></li></ul><hr><p>A \"Blue Wave\" come Election Day can boost stocks, but only after bouts of strong volatility and a knee-jerk decline, <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/ms-stock\">Morgan Stanley</a> strategists said Friday.</p><p>Current polls suggest Democratic presidential nominee Joe Biden will beat President Donald Trump in November, and that the Democratic Party holds a strong chance of securing control of Congress. Yet US equities are among the few assets poised for a \"detour\" should such a sweep take place, the bank said in a note to clients.</p><p>While some assets such as Treasurys and oil would face a steady decline, an overwhelming Democratic victory would form a temporary deviation from stocks' upward trajectory, they added.</p><p>The market's immediate reaction will likely be negative, according to the firm. Fears of tax hikes will drive initial selling and lower earnings outlooks. The continued economic recovery would drive some derating of earnings-per-share multiples, posing a short-term risk until profit growth catches up with the updated forecasts. Uncertainty around future stimulus can also cloud initial hopes for fresh relief, the bank said.</p><p><em><strong>Read more:</strong> <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/investing-strategy-and-stock-picks-from-fund-manager-brandon-nelson-2020-10\" data-analytics-position=\"3\" data-analytics-module=\"\">Fund manager Brandon Nelson is tripling his benchmark in 2020 with 'less-discovered' companies that become big winners. Here are 3 themes and 9 stocks he's betting on.</a></em></p><p>\"We expect fiscal expansion to provide some offset [to higher taxes], but until the market knows the type of fiscal expansion after a Democratic sweep, expect that equity risk premium could remain elevated into January,\" the team of strategists wrote.</p><p>Still, stocks should resume their climb once volatility dies down and investors get a clearer look at the Biden administration's legislative agenda, according to Morgan Stanley. The continuation of economic recovery will revive spending and drive earnings growth. A follow-up to the March CARES Act will lift bullishness, and Morgan Stanley expects the tax scare to give way to a smaller-than-expected increase.&#160;</p><p>\"Our base case is to buy any dip on a blue wave as we think tax policy is difficult to enact and think the legislative focus will lean toward CARES 2 as a top priority,\" the team said.</p><p>As for other outcomes, the bank views a divided government as having less of an up-front slump but a longer struggle with passing new stimulus. The nation's economic rebound could stall and slam investors' bullish forecasts, the strategists added.</p><p><em><strong>Now read more markets coverage from Markets Insider and Business 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Republican Jason Lewis challenges Sen. Tina Smith in Minnesota","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/minnesota-senate-race-tina-smith-vs-jason-lewis-2020","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f592d59e6ff30001d4e7d9f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Jason lewis\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>House Budget Committee member Rep. Jason Lewis, R-Minn. questions Budget Director Mick Mulvaney on Capitol Hill in Washington, on Capitol Hill in Washington, during the committee&#39;s hearing on President Donald Trump&#39;s fiscal 2018 federal budget.\n<p class=\"copyright\"><a href=\"http://www.apimages.com/metadata/Index/Trump-Budget/139d084d0d104267a367f2306adf0e4a/3/0\" target=\"_blank\">Jacquelyn Martin/AP</a></p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Democratic&#160;<strong>Sen. Tina Smith&#160;</strong>is running for a full term in the US Senate against Republican&#160;<strong>Jason Lewis in Minnesota.&#160;</strong></li>\n<li>\n<p>Smith was appointed to former <strong>Sen. Al Franken</strong>'s US Senate seat when he resigned from office in December 2017 and won a 2018 special election to serve out the rest of Franken's term until 2021.&#160;</p>\n</li>\n<li>Lewis, her Republican opponent, is a former talk radio host who previously represented Minnesota's 2nd Congressional District for one term.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Democratic&#160;<strong>Sen. Tina Smith&#160;</strong>is running for a full term in the US Senate against Republican&#160;<strong>Jason Lewis.&#160;</strong></p><h2><strong>The candidates:</strong></h2><p>Smith, Minnesota's former lieutenant governor, was appointed to former&#160;<strong>Sen. Al Franken</strong>'s US Senate seat when he resigned from office in December 2017 and won a 2018 special election to serve out the rest of Franken's term until 2021.&#160;</p><p>This fall, Smith is running for her first full term for the seat. She currently serves on four US Senate committees including the Committee on Banking, Housing, and Urban Affairs and the Committee on Health, Education, Labor, and Pensions (HELP).&#160;</p><p>In the Senate,&#160;<a href=\"https://www.smith.senate.gov/us-senator-tina-smith-fierce-advocate-minnesota\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\">she's heavily focused on healthcare issues,</a>&#160;including expanding coverage, reducing prescription drug costs, and combatting the opioid crisis in Minnesota.&#160;</p><p>Smith's opponent, Lewis, is a former talk radio host who previously represented Minnesota's 2nd Congressional District in the suburbs southeast of the Twin Cities area for one term from 2017 to 2019. He was unseated in 2018 by Democratic challenger&#160;<strong>Rep. Angie Craig.&#160;</strong></p><p>Lewis' campaign message has focused on revitalizing Minnesota's economy, particularly the mining communities in the state's Iron Range, protecting the 2nd Amendment, and supporting law enforcement.&#160;</p><h2><strong>The stakes:</strong></h2><p>In addition to winning back the White House, regaining control of the US Senate for the first time since 2015 is a top priority for Democrats and would be a major accomplishment towards either delivering on a future president Joe Biden's policy goals or thwarting President Donald Trump's second-term agenda.</p><p>Currently, the US Senate is made up of 53 Republicans, 45 Democrats, and two independents that caucus with Democrats, winning that Democrats need to win back a net total of four seats to have a 51-seat majority (if Biden wins, his vice president would also serve as president of the Senate and would be a tie-breaker vote).&#160;</p><p>In the 2018 midterm elections, Democrats flipped two Republican-controlled seats, the 2nd and 3rd Districts, in the Twin Cities seats, but lost control of two seats in rural Minnesota, the 1st District in the Southern part of the state and the 8th District in the mountainous Iron Range region in Northern Minnesota.&#160;</p><p>This year, Republicans hoping to build on their gains in 2018 in rural areas and are aiming to target Minnesota in both the electoral college and the Senate, but the state is still expected to favor Democrats. Democratic nominee Joe Biden leads Trump by over six percentage points on average in polls of the state, <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/polls/president-general/minnesota/\">according to FiveThirtyEight's polling average.&#160;</a></p><p><strong>The money race:&#160;</strong>Smith has substantially outraised and outspent Lewis in the cycle so far, <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=MNS1MNS1\">according to the Center for Responsive Politics</a>. She's brought in $10 million, spent $4.6 million, and has $5.8 million in cash on hand compared to $2.4 million raised, $1.5 million spent, and $992,607 in cash on hand for Lewis.&#160;</p><p><strong>What the polling says:&#160;</strong>The most recent poll of the race conducted by The New York Times and Siena College showed Smith <a href=\"https://int.nyt.com/data/documenttools/crosstabs-mn-nh-nv-wi/aefa3a3ec36370e9/full.pdf\">ahead of Lewis by nine points</a>, 49% to 40%. Another survey <a href=\"http://www.surveyusa.com/client/PollReport.aspx?g=cc902191-9d67-498a-aa9c-d59233e2c85b\">conducted by SurveyUSA</a> from September 4 to 7 showed Smith leading Lewis by 11 points, 47% to 36%. A previous poll <a href=\"https://www.publicpolicypolling.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/09/MinnesotaPoll9420.pdf\">conducted by Public Policy Polling</a> September 3 to 4 showed Smith leading Lewis by eight points, 49% to 41%.&#160;</p><p><strong>What some of the experts say:</strong> The <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/senate-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a> and <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/senate\">Inside Elections</a> rate the race between Smith and Lewis as \"safe Democratic\" while <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-senate/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball at the University of Virginia Center for Politics</a> rates it \"likely Democratic.\"&#160;</p><p>According to <a href=\"https://projects.fivethirtyeight.com/2020-election-forecast/senate/minnesota/\">FiveThirtyEight</a>, Smith has a 92% chance of winning her reelection bid in November. Smith is expected to receive 55% of the popular vote, or 13% more than Lewis.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5be23a7ed0ee001e25ef09?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Sara Jacobs California\" height=\"2000\" width=\"4000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Sara Jacobs Campaign</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Sara Jacobs and Georgette G&#243;mez will face off in November to represent California's 53rd Congressional District.</li>\n<li>California's 53rd Congressional District is located in western California entirely within San Diego County.</li>\n<li>Both candidates on the ballot are Democrats, made possible by California's \"top-two primary\" system which places the top two candidates in the state's primary on the November ballot.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Democrats <strong>Sara Jacobs</strong> and <strong>Georgette Gómez</strong>&#160;will face off in November to represent California's 53rd Congressional District in the House of Representatives.</p><p>California has a <a href=\"https://www.sos.ca.gov/elections/primary-elections-california/\">\"top-two primary\"</a> system, meaning that candidates of all party affiliations compete in the primary on the same ballot and the top two winners of the primary election go on the final ballot, regardless of their political party.</p><h2>The candidates</h2><p>Jacobs is the founder and chair of <a href=\"https://www.sandiegoforeverychild.org/\">San Diego for Every Child</a>, a nonprofit organization tackling childhood poverty in San Diego. She is also the founder of <a href=\"https://www.projectconnect.world/about\">Project Connect</a>, an education nonprofit which maps schools around the world. During the Obama administration, Jacobs spent time working in the U.S. State Department, and has also worked at UNICEF and the United Nations.&#160;</p><p>Her <a href=\"https://sarajacobsforca.com/issues\">campaign platform is centered around</a> fighting for racial justice and police reform, implementing a universal healthcare system, supporting small business, and expanding access to affordable housing in Southern California.</p><p>Gómez is the current president of the San Diego City Council, the first LGBT Latina to hold the position. From January 2018 to October 2019, she served as the chairwoman of the San Diego Metropolitan Transit System.</p><p>Gómez's <a href=\"https://georgettegomez.org/georgettes-bold-plan-for-america/\">campaign platform is focused on</a> economic justice policies including extending unemployment benefits until the COVID-19 pandemic is over, canceling federal student loan debt for middle and lower-income Americans, and investing in solutions to climate change.</p><h2>The district</h2><p>California's 53rd Congressional District is located in western California in San Diego County. It is home to the central and eastern regions of San Diego and portions of Chula Vista, El Cajon, and all of Bonita, La Mesa, Lemon Grove, and Spring Valley.</p><p>In the 2016 presidential election, the 53rd District overwhelmingly voted for Democratic nominee Hillary Clinton over President Donald Trump in a 65-30 percentage point split of the vote, <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2013/07/09/1220127/-Daily-Kos-Elections-2012-election-results-by-congressional-and-legislative-districts\">according to the Daily Kos</a>.</p><h2>The money race</h2><p>Campaign finance data from the <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=CA53CA53\">Center for Responsive Politics</a> shows that Jacobs has raised $3.6 million for her campaign so far, or over three times more than Gómez with $1.1 million. Gómez, however, currently has the cash on hand advantage over her opponent. Gómez currently has $264,503 left to spend on her campaign as the November election approaches — Jacobs has just $138,399 remaining.</p><h2>What experts say</h2><p>According to forecasting by <a href=\"https://forecast.decisiondeskhq.com/house/H2020CA53\">Decision Desk HQ</a>, Jacobs is favored in the race.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" Chris Pappas&#160;</strong>is running for a second term against Republican <strong>Matt Mowers&#160;</strong>in New Hampshire's 1st Congressional District.&#160;</li>\n<li>Mowers is a former diplomat and New Hampshire Republican Party executive director who served as an advisor in the US State Department.</li>\n<li>This district flipped from narrowly backing President Obama in 2012 to narrowly supporting President Trump in 2016.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>First-term Democratic <strong>Rep. Chris Pappas&#160;</strong>is running for a second term against Republican <strong>Matt Mowers&#160;</strong>in New Hampshire's 1st Congressional District.&#160;</p><h2>The candidates</h2><p>Pappas was elected in the 2018 midterms to replace retiring Democratic Rep. Carol Shea-Porter. He formerly served as a member of the New Hampshire Executive Council, which essentially functions as an advisory board to the governor's office, and helped run his family's small business.&#160;</p><p>In Congress, he serves on the Committee on Veterans Affairs and the Committee on Transportation and Infrastructure. His <a href=\"https://www.chrispappas.org/about-chris\">campaign platform</a> emphasizes improving healthcare and combatting the opioid epidemic, supporting New Hampshire's small businesses, and ensuring benefits for veterans.&#160;</p><p>Mowers is a former diplomat and New Hampshire Republican Party executive director who served as an advisor in the US State Department under President Donald Trump's administration and was endorsed by Trump in the primary.</p><p>On September 8, Mowers easily defeated his opponent Matt Mayberry in the GOP primary for the district. <a href=\"https://mattmowers.com/issues/\">His campaign platform</a> focuses on helping New Hampshire's economy recover from COVID-19, bolstering national security, protecting the 2nd Amendment, and establishing term limits for members of Congress.</p><h2>The district</h2><p>New Hampshire's 1st District occupies a chunk of the Eastern half of the state, including the cities and towns of Manchester, Merrimack, Laconia, Campton, Brentwood, and Dover.&#160;</p><p>From 2007 to 2019, control of the district flipped back and forth between two representatives, Republican Frank Guinta and Shea-Porter, nearly every cycle.&#160;</p><p>This swing district flipped from voting for former President Barack Obama by a margin of 1.6 percentage points in 2012 to voting for Trump also by a margin of 1.6 percentage points in 2016, <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2012/11/19/1163009/-Daily-Kos-Elections-presidential-results-by-congressional-district-for-the-2012-2008-elections\">according to Daily Kos.&#160;</a></p><h2>The money race</h2><p>The drawn-out primary, which wasn't resolved until early September, allowed Pappas to amass a significant cash advantage over Mowers. Pappas has raised $2.1 million this cycle and spent $750,000 compared to less than $700,000 raised and $318,000 spent for Mowers, <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=NH01NH01\">according to the Center for Responsive Politics.&#160;</a></p><h2>What some of the experts say</h2><p>The race between Pappas and Mowers is currently rated as&#160;\"likely Democratic\" by the <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report,</a>&#160;<a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections,</a> and <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball</a> at the University of Virginia Center for Politics.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-source=\"insider-voter-guide\" data-show-header=\"false\">Expanded Coverage Module: 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Republican Bob Good and Democrat Cameron Webb face off for Virginia's 5th Congressional src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f57c4ee7ed0ee001e25dfcf?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Cameron Webb\" height=\"959\" width=\"1918\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Cameron Webb\n<p class=\"copyright\">Screenshot via MSNBC</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Republican&#160;<strong>Bob Good&#160;</strong>and Democrat&#160;<strong>Dr. Cameron Webb&#160;</strong>are competing in the open race for Virginia's 5th Congressional District.</li>\n<li>Earlier this summer, Republicans in the district ousted current GOP Rep. Denver Riggleman and replaced him with Good.&#160;</li>\n<li>Webb <a href=\"https://med.virginia.edu/phs/viewpoints/team/https://med.virginia.edu/phs/viewpoints/team/\">is both a lawyer and a physician</a> who serves as Director of Health Policy and Equity at the University's School of Medicine and was a White House fellow from 2016 to 2017.&#160;</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Republican&#160;<strong>Bob Good&#160;</strong>and Democrat&#160;<strong>Dr. Cameron Webb&#160;</strong>are competing in the open race for Virginia's 5th Congressional District this fall.&#160;</p><h2>The candidates:</h2><p>The 2020 election is the third cycle in a row where the 5th District seat is open with no incumbent. In 2016, Republican Tom Garrett won election to the seat, but decided not to run for reelection. That year, current Rep. Denver Riggleman, a US Air Force veteran and distillery owner, defeated Democratic candidate Leslie Cockburn to win election to the seat.&#160;</p><p>Earlier this summer, <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/06/14/rep-denver-riggleman-ousted-in-virginia-gop-convention-316589\">Riggleman was ousted and failed to be renominated by his own party</a> in a drive-through convention over his support of same-sex marriage and his officiating a same-sex wedding in the summer of 2019, replacing him with Good.</p><p>In Virginia, congressional-district level political parties can choose their nominations in conventions as opposed to traditional state-run primary elections.&#160;</p><p>Good, a former member of the Campbell County Board of Supervisors, is more conservative than Riggleman. Notable in his primary win, he opposes same-sex marriage <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/virginia-politics/bob-good-cameron-webb-culture-wars/2020/08/23/d658b0ec-e3f9-11ea-b69b-64f7b0477ed4_story.html\">and equal rights for transgender Americans</a>, highlighting on his campaign website <a href=\"https://wset.com/news/local/campbell-county-board-of-supervisors-vote-to-move-against-transgender-bathrooms\">that he fought to pass a resolution in Campbell County</a> in 2016 restricting transgender and non-binary individuals from using public restrooms that match their gender as opposed to biological sex.&#160;</p><p>Good's <a href=\"https://www.bobgoodforcongress.com/bob-goods-proven-record/\">campaign platform</a> also emphasizes his work in local government reducing taxes and government spending, opposing abortion, and defending gun rights.&#160;</p><p>His Democratic opponent, Webb, <a href=\"https://med.virginia.edu/phs/viewpoints/team/https://med.virginia.edu/phs/viewpoints/team/\">is both a lawyer and a physician</a> currently practicing internal medicine at the University of Virginia and serving as Director of Health Policy and Equity at the University's School of Medicine. He served as a White House fellow working on policy issues including healthcare and criminal justice from 2016 to 2017 under both the Obama and Trump administrations.&#160;</p><p>Webb's <a href=\"https://www.drcameronwebb.com/health-and-healthcare\">campaign platform</a> emphasizes improving access to affordable healthcare and lowering prescription drug costs, bolstering government support for COVID-19 recovery efforts, and combatting climate change.&#160;</p><p>On <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DrCameronWebb\">his Twitter feed</a>, he's been documenting his work juggling running a congressional campaign, teaching a medical school course, and working shifts at the University of Virginia's hospital treating COVID-19 patients.&#160;</p><h2>The district:</h2><p>Virginia's 5th District <a href=\"https://www.govtrack.us/congress/members/VA/5\">encompasses a swath of Central Virginia</a>, stretching from Fauquier County in the Washington, DC suburbs to include the city of Charlottesville and then down to southern Virginia along the North Carolina border. It was first represented by James Madison from 1789 to 1793.&#160;</p><p>This district has traditionally voted Republican in recent cycles. In 2012, Republican presidential nominee Mitt Romney carried the district by a margin of over eight percentage points, and President Donald Trump carried the seat by a margin of 11 points in 2016, <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2012/11/19/1163009/-Daily-Kos-Elections-presidential-results-by-congressional-district-for-the-2012-2008-elections\">according to Daily Kos Elections.</a></p><p>In 2017, Republican gubernatorial nominee Ed Gillespie <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1yELTkkCm5arWa0VVt-V2pvnmFQc38qBL1Hq4ICHib10/edit#gid=962305598\">carried the district by a margin of nine points,</a> 54% to 45%, over Democratic Gov. Ralph Northam.&#160;</p><h2>The money race:</h2><p>Webb has significantly outraised and outspent Good, <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=VA05VA05\">according to the Center for Responsive Politics.</a> Webb has so far brought in $1.35 million, spent a little over $900,000, and has over $453,000 in cash on hand while Good has raised $261,000, spent over $193,000, and has $68,000 in cash on hand.&#160;</p><h2>What some of the experts say:&#160;</h2><p>The race between Good and Webb is rated as \"likely Republican\" by <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections,</a> and as a \"tossup\" by <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">The Cook Political Report</a> and <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball at the University of Virginia Center for Politics.</a>&#160;</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/5f5bc532e6ff30001d4e8646?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"f5121347e8fc4fd0d64c4b14e438027d","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn3@2020_5/2020/10/09/19-12-45-932_2a3dfce93971b2db.webp","destWidth":1443,"destHeight":1082,"sourceBytes":35086,"destBytes":35086,"author":"gpanetta@businessinsider.com (Grace Panetta)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5f57c4ee7ed0ee001e25dfcf?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn76@2020_6/2020/10/09/19-12-55-989_0fd88e559b2ef289.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn91@2020_3/2020/10/09/19-12-53-792_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zc_wE6ENG_o:y1_8SRo-Peg:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn29@2020_2/2020/10/09/19-12-51-353_94ec7d507c85c794.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zc_wE6ENG_o:y1_8SRo-Peg:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn43@2020_1/2020/10/09/19-12-54-205_c8f8ba11c9f413be.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn40@2020_6/2020/10/09/19-12-50-625_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zc_wE6ENG_o:y1_8SRo-Peg:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn85@2020_6/2020/10/09/19-12-52-425_f49662f70c586d8e.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/zc_wE6ENG_o":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn92@2020_4/2020/10/09/19-12-53-020_96c9d95f7e448fb6.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1602270691387},{"createdTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Canadian researchers gave $7,500 to people without a home — and the results show the power of universal basic income","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/canadian-basic-income-experiment-gives-homeless-people-cash-2020-10","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5e834d512ff8393d5b562a53?format=jpeg\" alt=\"siberia homeless\" height=\"998\" width=\"1500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The New Leaf project studied what would happen if people without a home were given a large cash infusion.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alexey Malgavko/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>The Foundation for Social Change, a Vancouver-based charity, partnered with the University of British Columbia to identify 50 people who had recently become homeless.</li>\n<li>Researchers gave them a <a href=\"https://www.newswire.ca/news-releases/a-global-first-direct-cash-transfer-study-shows-promising-results-for-people-recently-homeless-881750516.html\">one-time payment of $7,500</a> and studied their spending habits and living situation over the next 12 months.</li>\n<li>The recipients were able to secure stable housing faster than those who didn't receive the cash infusion, saving the shelter system $8,100 per person.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>A Canadian charity recently conducted a bold social experiment: giving people experiencing homelessness a one-time cash infusion of $7,500.</p><p>According to the researchers, the results were \"beautifully surprising.\"&#160;</p><p>The study, entitled <a href=\"https://static1.squarespace.com/static/5f07a92f21d34b403c788e05/t/5f751297fcfe7968a6a957a8/1601507995038/2020_09_30_FSC_Statement_of_Impact_w_Expansion.pdf\">the New Leaf project</a>, speaks to the power of an interim <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-basic-income-2016-8\">universal basic income</a> to lift people out of poverty. A universal basic income is essentially a cash handout from the government, often for the purposes of rehabilitating those in poverty.</p><p>More jurisdictions across the world are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/scotland-government-to-seriously-consider-universal-basic-income-2020-5\">experimenting with the policy</a>, including the US's recent trial in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/andrew-yang-universal-basic-income-cash-experiment-upstate-new-york-2020-5\">upstate New York</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/kenya-village-disproving-biggest-myth-about-basic-income-2017-12\">the ongoing study</a> run by the NGO GiveDirectly in Kenyan villages.&#160;</p><p>The Foundation for Social Change, a Vancouver-based charity, partnered with the University of British Columbia to identify 50 people between 19 and 64 years old who had recently become homeless. The recipients were identified as not having significant substance abuse or mental health issues.</p><p>Researchers <a href=\"https://static1.squarespace.com/static/5f07a92f21d34b403c788e05/t/5f751297fcfe7968a6a957a8/1601507995038/2020_09_30_FSC_Statement_of_Impact_w_Expansion.pdf\">studied their spending habits</a> over 12 months and compared their outcomes to a control group who did not receive the cash payment.&#160;</p><p>Those who were given the cash largely spent the money on food, rent, and transportation and moved into stable housing faster over the course of the year, according to the <a href=\"https://www.newswire.ca/news-releases/a-global-first-direct-cash-transfer-study-shows-promising-results-for-people-recently-homeless-881750516.html\">findings</a>. Spending on \"temptation goods,\" such as drugs, cigarettes, and alcohol declined by 39%, on average. And recipients were able to keep an average of $1,000 in savings, according to Canadian news outlet <a href=\"https://www.cbc.ca/news/canada/british-columbia/new-leaf-project-results-1.5752714\">CBC</a>.&#160;</p><p>The cash payment saved the shelter system $8,100 per person over the course of the year, a total savings of $405,000.</p><p>It also gave some participants the chance to update their job skills.&#160;</p><p>\"When I found out I had been accepted to receive the cash transfer, I was living in an emergency shelter, trying to find a way forward,\" a New Leaf project participant whose identity was kept anonymous said in a press release. \"The money gave me the resources I needed to get out of the shelter and push for the social programs and the computer class I needed. It was an important stepping-stone and it gave me a choice. It gave me a chance.\"&#160;</p><p>Eventually, the Foundation for Social Change hopes to <a href=\"https://forsocialchange.org/new-leaf-project-overview\">expand the study</a> with a $10 million fundraising effort, to deliver the same impact to many more people across Canada.</p><p>\"Homelessness can happen to anyone,\" Williams wrote in the study's impact statement, noting that many people are just one paycheck away from losing their homes or cars, and being forced to find other ways of living. \"While the economic impact of homelessness costs everyone, ultimately it is the human cost that is so devastating.\"</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/canadian-basic-income-experiment-gives-homeless-people-cash-2020-10'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=4iw_GcB4aVk:BDmN_UtFPjM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=4iw_GcB4aVk:BDmN_UtFPjM:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Four-term incumbent Rep. Mike Turner squares off against Desiree Tims in Ohio's 10th Congressional District.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/ohio-10th-district-house-election-mike-turner-desiree-tims-2020","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f5fd6ad57b7da001ee1187c?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mike Turner\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">AP Photo/J. Scott Applewhite</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Four-term incumbent Rep. Mike Turner will face Democrat Desiree Tims in Ohio's 10th Congressional District.</li>\n<li>The district is located in western Ohio and includes the city of Dayton, as well as Montgomery, Greene, and Fayette counties.</li>\n<li>Tims has received endorsements from President Barack Obama, 2020 Democratic presidential nominee Joe Biden, and Vice Presidential nominee Kamala Harris.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Four-term incumbent <strong>Rep. Mike Turner</strong> faces off against Democrat <strong>Desiree Tims</strong> in Ohio's 10th Congressional District.</p><h2>The candidates</h2><p>Turner is a lawyer and has represented the 10th District since 2003. He previously served as the mayor of Dayton, a position he served in for two terms from 1994 to 2002.</p><p>In Congress, Turner sits on the House Committee on Armed Services, where he is a ranking member in the Strategic Forces subcommittee, and on the House Permanent Select Committee on Intelligence. He also served as President of the North Atlantic Treaty Organization's Parliamentary Assembly, which includes lawmakers from NATO member nations, from 2014 to 2016.&#160;&#160;</p><p>Tims, Turner's Democratic challenger, is a former Capitol Hill staffer for Sen. Sherrod Brown and Sen. Kirsten Gillibrand. During her time working in Congress, she was elected by the Senate Black Legislative Staff Caucus to become the group's president.</p><p>Tims says she's running for Congress to expand the representation of Americans from low-income backgrounds like herself and fight for their interests in Congress.&#160;</p><p>\"I get very passionate about it, because it's very frustrating when you see that up close, the neglect that is consistent in the halls of Congress,\" <a href=\"https://www.buzzfeednews.com/article/henrygomez/desiree-tims-dayton-ohio-democrat-congress\">Tims told Buzzfeed News</a> for a profile published in July. \"So instead of begging and advocating people to do the right thing, let's just replace them.\"</p><p>Tims has received endorsements from President Barack Obama, Sen. Brown, Vice Presidential nominee Kamala Harris, Sen. Gillibrand, and Rep. Marcia Fudge. Her <a href=\"https://timsforcongress.com/issues/\">campaign platform is centered on</a> establishing a national universal preschool program, opposing \"right-to-work\" laws, criminal justice reform, and combatting gun violence with measures including banning assault weapons.</p><h2>The district</h2><p>Ohio's 10th Congressional District is located in the western region of the state and is home to the counties of Montgomery, Greene, and Fayette. The district also includes the entire city of Dayton.</p><p>This district has been reliably Republican in the past few election cycles. In the 2016 presidential election, the district voted for President Donald Trump over Democratic nominee Hillary Clinton in a 51-44 percentage point split of the vote, <a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2013/7/9/1220127/-Daily-Kos-Elections-2012-election-results-by-congressional-and-legislative-districts\">according to Daily Kos</a>.</p><h2>The money race</h2><p>According to the <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=OH10OH10\">Center for Responsive Politics</a>, Turner has raised $1.1 million for his campaign, spent $592,000, and currently has $576,834 in cash on hand. His opponent, Tims, has raised about $597,000, spent $260,000, and has $336,000 remaining to spend as the November election approaches.</p><h2>What some of the experts say</h2><p>The race between Turner and Tims is rated as \"likely Republican\" by <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections</a>, the <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">Cook Political Report</a>, and <a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball</a> at the University of Virginia Center for Politics.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-source=\"insider-voter-guide\" data-show-header=\"false\">Expanded Coverage Module: 03:11:31","updatedTime":"2020-10-10 03:11:31","title":"Madison Cawthorn faces off against Moe Davis in North Carolina's 11th Congressional District","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/north-carolina-11th-district-house-election-madison-cawthorn-moe-davis-2020","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f471359cd2fec00296a4749?format=jpeg\" alt=\"madison cawthorn convention speech\" height=\"1249\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Madison Cawthorn\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo Courtesy of the Committee on Arrangements for the 2020 Republican National Committee via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Republican Madison Cawthorn and Democrat Moe Davis are facing off to replace Mark Meadows in North Carolina's 11th Congressional District.&#160;</li>\n<li>Cawthorn, 25, is a motivational speaker, investor, and staunch supporter of President Trump positioning himself as the voice of the next generation of the GOP.&#160;</li>\n<li>\n<p>North Carolina's 11th district is located in the Western part of the state and has traditionally leaned Republican but was recently redrawn, following a court order, to be slightly more favorable to Democrats.</p>\n</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider's homepage for more stories</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Republican&#160;<strong>Madison Cawthorn&#160;</strong>and Democrat&#160;<strong>Morris \"Moe\" Davis&#160;</strong>are competing in the race to replace former Rep. Mark Meadows, who left Congress to serve as White House chief of staff, in North Carolina's 11th Congressional District.&#160;</p><h2>The candidates:</h2><p>Cawthorn, who just turned 25 on August 1, made national headlines <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/madison-cawthorn-24-beats-trump-pick-in-north-carolina-primary-2020-6\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"20\" data-uri=\"b3050a4d34b098d2929a6877471e7410\">when he defeated realtor Lynda Bennett</a>, Meadows' hand-picked candidate for the seat who had also been endorsed by President Donald Trump, by over 30 points in a June 23 primary runoff.</p><p>Cawthorn became an investor and motivational speaker after being paralyzed in a car accident in 2014. Since winning his primary runoff, Cawthorn has quickly gained a massive following on social media and been branded as a rising star in the GOP, earning a coveted speaking slot at the Republican National Convention.&#160;</p><p>Cawthorn, who would be the youngest member of the US House if elected, has also positioned himself both as a counterweight to the burgeoning youth progressive moment and as bridge between the GOP's leadership and the next generation of Republicans in Generation Z. In addition to speaking at the RNC, he's made frequent appearances on Fox News and doing interviews with prominent conservative figures <a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CCHUGinjbZq/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"68de40e09e11220de553d0941227a576\">including Glenn Beck</a>&#160;<a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CDPtI83Db0L/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"fd1b104443190ddf92ca700845edcf2e\">and Charlie Kirk.&#160;</a></p><p>Davis, 59, is a retired Air Force colonel&#160;<a href=\"https://moedavisforcongress.com/meet-moe/\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"125310e586e2199fae712b0c16faf84d\">who had a 25-year career in the military</a>. He worked on national security issues under both the Bush and Obama administrations, including as a Chief Prosecutor at Guantanamo Bay, and more recently has been a Howard University Law Professor.</p><p>An&#160;<a href=\"https://twitter.com/ColMorrisDavis\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"40\" data-uri=\"f9337a8241338b9b4e43a3dbc9b398cb\">ardent Trump critic on social media</a>, Davis is highlighting the need to expand affordable healthcare, improve education, and invest in infrastructure in Western North Carolina&#160;<a href=\"https://moedavisforcongress.com/moes-vision/#healthcare\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"4374397177f1a1f625cddd94d26122d5\">in his campaign platform.</a></p><h2>The district:</h2><p>North Carolina's 11th district is located in the Western part of the state and has traditionally leaned Republican.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.npr.org/2019/09/16/760177030/a-surprise-vote-thrown-phone-and-partisan-mistrust-roil-n-c-as-maps-are-redrawn\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"db6fbb00b09523032fe861d34dd611d3\">A court ordered the North Carolina legislature to redraw its entire congressional district maps in 2019</a>, ruling that the previous map unfairly favored Republicans. In addition&#160;<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2019/12/03/north-carolinas-new-congressional-map-shifts-two-seats-toward-democrats/?arc404=true\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"6bf8328540f6596a6bfda4a5f6d63ba0\">to creating two new likely Democratic districts</a>, the redistricting others, like the 11th district, slightly more favorable to Democrats.&#160;</p><p>While the 11th is still solidly in the Republican column, its new boundaries <a href=\"https://www.bpr.org/post/nc11-cawthorn-takes-hard-right-turn#stream/0\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"70ce25b7fb0b2a79c3fd53263a763b5f\">now include all of Buncombe County,&#160;</a>which is home to the Democratic-leaning city of Asheville&#160;<a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/elections/2016/results/north-carolina\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"729fff00bf94e3b48616288abcf2e05d\">and voted for Clinton by 14 points</a>&#160;in 2016.&#160;</p><p>Trump&#160;<a href=\"https://www.dailykos.com/stories/2012/11/19/1163009/-Daily-Kos-Elections-presidential-results-by-congressional-district-for-the-2012-2008-elections\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"5f1d181a742686c409d5b5740785019c\">would have carried the district under its new, current lines by 17 points</a>, 57% to 40% over Hillary Clinton in 2016, and Meadows&#160;<a href=\"https://ballotpedia.org/North_Carolina%27s_11th_Congressional_District_election,_2018\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"60\" data-uri=\"8c3da3d4816323a855affe22e9851155\">won re-election by over 20 points in 2018.&#160;</a></p><h2>The money race:</h2><p>Cawthorn has raised a little over $800,000 and spent $638,000, <a href=\"https://www.opensecrets.org/races/summary?cycle=2020&id=NC11NC11\">according to the Center for Responsive Politics</a>, compared to around $488,000 raised and $220,00 spent for Davis. Morris, however, leads Cawthorn in cash on hand with nearly $268,000 in the bank compared to&#160;</p><h2>What some of the experts say:</h2><p><a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\"></a><a href=\"http://centerforpolitics.org/crystalball/2020-house/\">Sabato's Crystal Ball at the University of Virginia Center for Politics</a> rates the race between Cawthorn and Davis as \"likely Republican,\" <a href=\"https://insideelections.com/ratings/house\">Inside Elections</a> rates it as \"safe Republican,\" and <a href=\"https://cookpolitical.com/ratings/house-race-ratings\">the Cook Political Report</a> rates it as \"leans Republican.\"</p><bi-shortcode id=\"expanded-coverage\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f763a4374fe5b0018a8e962?format=jpeg\" alt=\"NYSE Trader\" height=\"999\" width=\"1999\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Traders look on after trading was halted on the floor of the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) in New York, U.S., March 18, 2020\n<p class=\"copyright\">Lucas Jackson/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul><li><strong>JPMorgan Private Bank's Monica DiCenso
